<div class="we"><div id="IMSLP34584" class="we_file_first we_fileblock_19">

</li></ul>

</dd><dd>II. Fuga: Sostenuto e legato
</dd><dd>III. Finale: Andante

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Misc._Comments">Misc. Comments</span></h2>
<h4> <span class="mw-headline" id="Publication_History">Publication History</span></h4>
<ul><li> Leipzig&#160;: Breitkopf &amp; Härtel, 1845 (<span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://anno.onb.ac.at/cgi-content/anno-buch?apm=0&amp;aid=1000001&amp;bd=0001845&amp;teil=0203&amp;seite=00000189&amp;zoom=1">Hofmeister's <i>Monatsbericht</i> (1845), p.189</a></span>) (also by Coventry &amp; Hollier in London, Maurice Schlesinger of Paris, and Ricordi of Milan, simultaneously)
</li></ul>
<dl><dd>Reprinted
<ul><li>Mineola: Dover Publications, 1991, 2004
</li></ul>
</dd></dl>
<ul><li> New York&#160;: G. Schirmer, 1896: <i>Compositions for the organ&#160;: three preludes and fugues, op. 37; six sonatas, op. 65 / Felix Mendelssohn Bartholdy. Edited and fingered by Samuel P. Warren</i>. Plate 12572 
</li><li> Paris&#160;: S. Bornemann, 1948: <i>Oeuvres complètes pour orgue / de Félix Mendelssohn&#160;; revues, annotées et doigtées par Marcel Dupré</i>
</li><li> München&#160;: G. Henle Verlag, 1976: <i>Orgelsonaten&#160;: opus 65 / Mendelssohn Bartholdy&#160;; nach Eigenschriften, Abschriften und den beiden Erstausgaben hrsg. von Hubert Meister&#160;; Finger- und Pedalsatz von Wolfgang Stockmeier</i>
</li></ul>
<p>A 3-movement early version of Op.65 no.3 exists in autograph manuscript at SBBerlin.
</p><p>Op.65 No.2 reuses a postlude (the <i><a href="/wiki/Nachspiel_in_D_major,_MWV_W_12_(Mendelssohn,_Felix)" title="Nachspiel in D major, MWV W 12 (Mendelssohn, Felix)">Nachspiel in D major</a></i>, MWV W 12) composed in Rome in 1831, according to Todd (<i>Mendelssohn: A Life in Music</i>, p.487). Composition and revision of the sonatas continued well into 1845. - Schissel
</p>
